00001  ; Alicie, 2022, based on original work by "Keith".
00002  
00003      .OPT Proc65816
00004  
00005  ; Definitions used in sending info about the monitor (debug command 4).
00006    0058              BOARD_ID                    = $58
00007    7E00              WORK_RAM_START              = $7E00
00008    7EE4              SHADOW_VECTOR_START         = $7EE4
00009    001C              SHADOW_VECTOR_SIZE          = $01C
00010    8000              MONITOR_CODE_START          = $8000
00011    FFE4              CPU_VECTOR_START            = $FFE4
00012    7F00              HW_IO_START                 = $7F00
00013    0100              HW_IO_SIZE                  = $0100
00014    FFFFFF            HW_BRK_ADDR                 = $FFFFFF
00015  
00016  ; Zero-page variables that are temporarily used when executing commands
00017  ; from the debugger. When the monitor is entered, their values are saved
00018  ; into the ZP save area in work RAM (RAM_ZP_SAVE), and restored before
00019  ; control is returned to the user's program, so their use by the debugger
00020  ; and monitor is transparent to the user.
00021    0000              DBG_VAR_00                  = $00
00022    0001              DBG_VAR_01                  = $01
00023    0002              DBG_VAR_02                  = $02
00024    0003              DBG_VAR_03                  = $03
00025    0004              DBG_VAR_04                  = $04
00026  
00027  ; Save-area in work-RAM for A.
00028    7E00              RAM_A_SAVE                  = $7E00
00029  
00030  ; Save-area in work-RAM for X.
00031    7E02              RAM_X_SAVE                  = $7E02
00032  
00033  ; Save-area in work-RAM for Y.
00034    7E04              RAM_Y_SAVE                  = $7E04
00035  
00036  ; Save-area in work-RAM for PC.
00037    7E06              RAM_PC_SAVE                 = $7E06
00038  
00039  ; Save-area in work-RAM for DP.
00040    7E08              RAM_DP_SAVE                 = $7E08
00041  
00042  ; Save-area in work-RAM for the stack pointer.
00043    7E0A              RAM_SP_SAVE                 = $7E0A
00044  
00045  ; Save-area in work-RAM for the P register.
00046    7E0C              RAM_P_SAVE                  = $7E0C
00047  
00048  ; Save-area in work-RAM for the emulation bit. This can be thought of
00049  ; as an extenstion bit to P. If E=1, the CPU is in emulation mode.
00050    7E0D              RAM_E_SAVE                  = $7E0D
00051  
00052  ; Save-area in work-RAM for the PB register.
00053    7E0E              RAM_PB_SAVE                 = $7E0E
00054  
00055  ; Save-area in work-RAM for the DB register.
00056    7E0F              RAM_DB_SAVE                 = $7E0F
00057  
00058  ; The auto-detected CPU type (0=65C02, 1=65816).
00059    7E10              RAM_CPU_TYPE                = $7E10
00060  
00061  ; 1 if the the monitor is currently being executed, 0 if user code.
00062    7E11              RAM_IN_MONITOR              = $7E11
00063  
00064  ; Why control has returned to the ROM monitor:
00065  ;    2: A BRK instruction was executed.
00066  ;    7: An NMI was generated.
00067    7E13              RAM_ENTER_MONITOR_REASON    = $7E13
00068  
00069  ; Five-byte area where $00-$04 are saved.
00070    7E14              RAM_ZP_SAVE                 = $7E14
00071  
00072  ; Flag variable at $7E19 of unknown use. It only ever gets set to 0.
00073    7E19              RAM_VAR_7E19                = $7E19
00074  
00075  ; Variable at $7E1A of unknown use. It gets set to 0, and apparently not used.
00076    7E1A              RAM_VAR_7E1A                = $7E1A
00077  
00078  ; Save-area in work-RAM for the system VIA's registers.
00079    7E1C              RAM_PCR_SAVE                = $7E1C
00080    7E1D              RAM_DDRB_SAVE               = $7E1D
00081    7E1E              RAM_DDRA_SAVE               = $7E1E
00082  
00083  ; Vectors in RAM which are called directly from the vectors in FLASH.
00084  ; These vectors are typically not overridden by the user, since they
00085  ; perform critical system and debugger operations.
00086    7E70              IRQ_02_ENTRY_VECTOR         = $7E70
00087    7E72              NMI_02_ENTRY_VECTOR         = $7E72
00088    7E74              BRK_816_ENTRY_VECTOR        = $7E74
00089    7E76              NMI_816_ENTRY_VECTOR        = $7E76
00090  
00091  ; Shadow vectors for 816 mode, which the user may set to hook the vector.
00092    7EE4              SHADOW_VEC_COP_816          = $7EE4
00093    7EE6              SHADOW_VEC_BRK_816          = $7EE6 ; unused?
00094    7EE8              SHADOW_VEC_ABORT_816        = $7EE8
00095    7EEA              SHADOW_VEC_NMI_816          = $7EEA ; unused?
00096    7EEC              SHADOW_VEC_RSVD_816         = $7EEC ; unused?
00097    7EEE              SHADOW_VEC_IRQ_816          = $7EEE
00098  
00099  ; Shadow vectors for the 65816 running in '02 emulation mode.
00100    7EF0              SHADOW_VEC_RSVD1_02         = $7EF0 ; unused
00101    7EF2              SHADOW_VEC_RSVD2_02         = $7EF2 ; unused
00102    7EF4              SHADOW_VEC_COP_02           = $7EF4
00103    7EF6              SHADOW_VEC_RSVD3_02         = $7EF6 ; unused
00104    7EF8              SHADOW_VEC_ABORT_02         = $7EF8
00105  
00106  ; Shadow vectors for all 65xx processors.
00107    7EFA              SHADOW_VEC_NMI_02           = $7EFA ; unused
00108    7EFC              SHADOW_VEC_RESET_02         = $7EFC ; unused
00109    7EFE              SHADOW_VEC_IRQ_02           = $7EFE
00110  
00111  ; IO for the VIA which is used for the USB debugger interface.
00112  ; Unused registers are commented-out.
00113    7FE0              SYSTEM_VIA_IOB              = $7FE0 ; Port B IO register
00114    7FE1              SYSTEM_VIA_IOA              = $7FE1 ; Port A IO register
00115    7FE2              SYSTEM_VIA_DDRB             = $7FE2 ; Port B data direction register
00116    7FE3              SYSTEM_VIA_DDRA             = $7FE3 ; Port A data direction register
00117  ;SYSTEM_VIA_T1C_L           = $7FE4 ; Timer 1 counter/latches, low-order
00118  ;SYSTEM_VIA_T1C_H           = $7FE5 ; Timer 1 high-order counter
00119  ;SYSTEM_VIA_T1L_L           = $7FE6 ; Timer 1 low-order latches
00120  ;SYSTEM_VIA_T1L_H           = $7FE7 ; Timer 1 high-order latches
00121  ;SYSTEM_VIA_T2C_L           = $7FE8 ; Timer 2 counter/latches, lower-order
00122  ;SYSTEM_VIA_T2C_H           = $7FE9 ; Timer 2 high-order counter
00123  ;SYSTEM_VIA_SR              = $7FEA ; Shift register
00124    7FEB              SYSTEM_VIA_ACR              = $7FEB ; Auxilliary control register
00125    7FEC              SYSTEM_VIA_PCR              = $7FEC ; Peripheral control register
00126  ;SYSTEM_VIA_IFR             = $7FED ; Interrupt flag register
00127  ;SYSTEM_VIA_IER             = $7FEE ; Interrupt enable register
00128  ;SYSTEM_VIA_ORA_IRA         = $7FEF ; Port A IO register, but no handshake
00129  
00130          ; FLASH contents start here.
00131  008000                        .ORG $8000
00132  
00133  Monitor_Start:
00134          .byte   "WDC"
00135          .BYTE   $FF
00136  
00137  Signature_String:
00138          .byte   $82,"$",$01,$FF
00139  
00140  Monitor_Version_String:
00141          .byte   "WDC65c816SK WDCMON Version =  2"
00142          .byte   ".0.4.3Version Date = Wed Mar 26"
00143          .byte   " 2014  2:46", $00
00144  
00145          ; Unused data in the monitor version string area.
00146          .byte   $FF,$FF,$FF,$FF,$FF,$FF,$FF,$FF
00147          .byte   $FF,$FF,$FF,$FF,$FF,$FF,$FF,$FF
00148          .byte   $FF,$FF,$FF,$FF,$FF,$FF,$FF,$FF
00149          .byte   $FF,$FF,$FF,$FF,$FF,$FF,$FF,$FF
00150          .byte   $FF,$FF,$FF,$FF,$FF,$FF,$FF,$FF
00151          .BYTE   $FF,$FF,$FF,$FF,$FF,$FF
00152  
00153  008080                        .ORG $8080
00154  ; A table of important pointers. This is located at address $8080, and
00155  ; is 128 bytes long in total, but not all of it is used. Not sure if the
00156  ; debugger uses this table for any reason, but user applications could
00157  ; use it, for example, to read and write to the USB FIFO.
00158  Pointer_Table:
00159  
00160      ; Used entries in the pointer table.
00161          .WORD   Signature_String
00162          .WORD   Initialize_System
00163          .WORD   Is_VIA_USB_RX_Data_Avail
00164          .WORD   Sys_VIA_USB_Char_RX
00165          .WORD   Sys_VIA_USB_Char_TX
00166          .WORD   RAM_IN_MONITOR
00167          .WORD   Monitor_Version_String
00168          .WORD   IRQ_02_ENTRY_VECTOR
00169          .WORD   IRQ_02_Entry_Vector_Default
00170          .WORD   NMI_02_Entry_Vector_Default
00171          .WORD   BRK_816_Entry_Vector_Default
00172          .WORD   NMI_816_Entry_Vector_Default
00173  
00174          ; Unused entries in the pointer table.
00175          .WORD   $FFFF, $FFFF, $FFFF, $FFFF
00176          .WORD   $FFFF, $FFFF, $FFFF, $FFFF
00177          .WORD   $FFFF, $FFFF, $FFFF, $FFFF
00178          .WORD   $FFFF, $FFFF, $FFFF, $FFFF
00179          .WORD   $FFFF, $FFFF, $FFFF, $FFFF
00180          .WORD   $FFFF, $FFFF, $FFFF, $FFFF
00181          .WORD   $FFFF, $FFFF, $FFFF, $FFFF
00182          .WORD   $FFFF, $FFFF, $FFFF, $FFFF
00183          .WORD   $FFFF, $FFFF, $FFFF, $FFFF
00184          .WORD   $FFFF, $FFFF, $FFFF, $FFFF
00185          .WORD   $FFFF, $FFFF, $FFFF, $FFFF
00186          .WORD   $FFFF, $FFFF, $FFFF, $FFFF
00187          .WORD   $FFFF, $FFFF, $FFFF, $FFFF
00188  
00189  008100                        .ORG $8100
00190  
00191  ; Called directly from FLASH vector on IRQ in emulation mode. IRQ and BRK
00192  ; are shared in this mode, so jump to monitor code which checks for BRK.
00193  IRQ_02_entry:
00194  008100  6C 70 7E              jmp     (IRQ_02_ENTRY_VECTOR)
00195  008103  EA                    NOP
00196  
00197  ; Called directly from FLASH vector on NMI in emulation mode. Jump to monitor
00198  ; code to break into the debugger.
00199  NMI_02_entry:
00200  008104  6C 72 7E              jmp     (NMI_02_ENTRY_VECTOR)
00201  008107  EA                    NOP
00202  
00203  ; Called directly from FLASH vector on BRK in 816 mode. Jump to monitor
00204  ; code to break into the debugger.
00205  BRK_816_entry:
00206  008108  6C 74 7E              jmp     (BRK_816_ENTRY_VECTOR)
00207  00810B  EA                    NOP
00208  
00209  ; Called directly from FLASH vector on NMI in 816 mode. Jump to monitor
00210  ; code to break into the debugger.
00211  NMI_816_entry:
00212  00810C  6C 76 7E              jmp     (NMI_816_ENTRY_VECTOR)
00213  00810F  EA                    NOP
00214  
00215  ; Called directly from FLASH vector on COP in emulation mode. Call the
00216  ; user's handler through the shadow vector.
00217  COP_02_entry:
00218  008110  6C F4 7E              jmp     (SHADOW_VEC_COP_02)
00219  
00220  ; Called directly from FLASH vector on ABORT in emulation mode. Call the
00221  ; user's handler through the shadow vector.
00222  ABORT_02_entry:
00223  008113  6C F8 7E              jmp     (SHADOW_VEC_ABORT_02)
00224  
00225  ; Called directly from FLASH vector on IRQ in 816 mode.
00226  ; BRK and IRQ are separate in 816 mode, so no need to run any monitor code.
00227  ; Simply invoke the user's IRQ handler through the shadow vector.
00228  IRQ_816_entry:
00229  008116  6C EE 7E              jmp     (SHADOW_VEC_IRQ_816)
00230  
00231  ; Called directly from FLASH vector on ABORT in 816 mode.
00232  ABORT_816_entry:
00233  008119  6C E8 7E              jmp     (SHADOW_VEC_ABORT_816)
00234  
00235  ; Called directly from FLASH vector on COP in 816 mode.
00236  COP_816_entry:
00237  00811C  6C E4 7E              jmp     (SHADOW_VEC_COP_816)
00238  
00239  ; Does nothing forever. Called directly from several reserved vectors, and
00240  ; is also the default handler for all shadow vectors.
00241  Infinite_Loop:
00242  00811F  20 73 86              jsr     Do_Nothing_Subroutine_3
00243  008122  80 FB                 BRA     Infinite_Loop
00244  
00245  ; Does nothing forever. Called directly from a reserved vector.
00246  Infinite_Loop_2:
00247  008124  E2 20                 SEP     #$20    ; Set A to 8-bit.
00248  008126  20 73 86              jsr     Do_Nothing_Subroutine_3
00249  008129  80 F9                 BRA     Infinite_Loop_2
00250  
00251  ; Called directly from FLASH vector on RESET. Always executed in emulation mode.
00252  RESET_entry:
00253          ; Save the CPU context, init vectors, and switch into emulation mode.
00254  00812B  20 31 81              JSR     Initialize_Upon_Reset
00255  
00256          ; Save a copy of ZP memory, and sync up with the debugger.
00257  00812E  4C DB 81              jmp     Save_ZP_Sync_With_Debugger
00258  
00259  ; Called in emulation mode when the CPU is reset.
00260  Initialize_Upon_Reset:
00261          ; Push processor status on stack. The stack is not initialized yet,
00262          ; but Continue_System_Init expects P and A to be pushed on the stack,
00263          ; and we know the stack will be somewhere in page 1, so there will be
00264          ; RAM there to support it.
00265  008131  08                    PHP
00266  
00267          ; Set A to 8-bit mode. But why? We know we're in emulation mode here.
00268  008132  E2 20                 SEP	#$20
00269  
00270          ; Push A, load A with 1, and continue with initialization.
00271  008134  48                    pha
00272  008135  A9 01                 lda     #$01
00273  008137  80 04                 BRA     Continue_System_Init
00274  
00275  ; Called to initialize the system. The only place this is explicitly called
00276  ; is from Initialize_Upon_Reset, which is executed in emulation mode when the
00277  ; CPU is reset. But, there is a pointer to this function in the data pointer
00278  ; table, so perhaps the debugger calls it to reset the system. As such, this
00279  ; function ensures it works correctly even if called from native mode.
00280  Initialize_System:
00281          ; Push processor status on stack.
00282  008139  08                    PHP
00283  
00284          ; Set A to 8-bit mode and push it.
00285  00813A  E2 20                 SEP     #$20
00286  00813C  48                    PHA
00287  
00288  ; If called from an actual RESET, the CPU will be in emulation mode. If called
00289  ; through the data pointer table, the CPU may be in native mode with 8-bit A.
00290  ; Upon return, the CPU will be in emulation mode.
00291  Continue_System_Init:
00292  
00293          ; Disable interrupts and clear the decimal flag.
00294  00813D  78                    SEI
00295  00813E  D8                    CLD
00296  
00297          ; Zero a couple of variables whose use is currently unknown.
00298  00813F  9C 1A 7E              stz     RAM_VAR_7E1A
00299  008142  9C 19 7E              STZ     RAM_VAR_7E19
00300  
00301          ; Switch to native mode.
00302  008145  18                    clc
00303  008146  FB                    XCE
00304  
00305          ; Set XY to 16-bit mode and save them into the RAM save area.
00306  008147  C2 10                 REP     #$10
00307  008149  8E 02 7E              stx     RAM_X_SAVE
00308  00814C  8C 04 7E              STY     RAM_Y_SAVE
00309  
00310          ; Set A and XY to 8-bit mode.
00311  00814F  E2 30                 SEP     #$30
00312  
00313          ; Pull the prior value of A (8-bits) into X, and P into Y.
00314  008151  FA                    plx
00315  008152  7A                    PLY
00316  
00317          ; Save the processor status byte into the RAM save area.
00318  008153  8C 0C 7E              STY     RAM_P_SAVE
00319  
00320          ; Push 8-bit A back onto the stack.
00321  008156  48                    PHA
00322  
00323          ; Move the prior 8-bit value of A from X back into A.
00324  008157  8A                    TXA
00325  
00326          ; Set A to 16-bit mode.
00327  008158  C2 20                 REP     #$20
00328  
00329          ; Save A (all 16 bits) into the RAM save area.
00330  00815A  8F 00 7E 00           STA     \3RAM_A_SAVE
00331  
00332          ; Save DP (16 bits) into the RAM save area.
00333  00815E  7B                    TDC
00334  00815F  8F 08 7E 00           STA     \3RAM_DP_SAVE
00335  008163  3B                    TSC
00336  
00337          ; Save the 16-bit stack pointer into the RAM save area.
00338  008164  18                    CLC
00339  008165  69 03 00              ADC     \2#$03
00340  008168  8F 0A 7E 00           STA     \3RAM_SP_SAVE
00341  
00342          ; Set A and XY to 8-bit mode.
00343  00816C  E2 30                 SEP     #$30
00344  
00345          ; Save the 8-bit program bank into the RAM save area.
00346  00816E  4B                    PHK
00347  00816F  68                    pla
00348  008170  8F 0E 7E 00           STA     \3RAM_PB_SAVE
00349  
00350          ; Save the 8-bit data bank into the RAM save area.
00351  008174  8B                    PHB
00352  008175  68                    PLA
00353  008176  8F 0F 7E 00           STA     \3RAM_DB_SAVE
00354  
00355          ; Save the emulation mode flag into the RAM save area. Note it gets
00356          ; saved as "1", which means the CPU will be in emulation mode once
00357          ; the context is restored and the user's code is executed.
00358  00817A  A9 01                 lda     #$01
00359  00817C  8F 0D 7E 00           STA     \3RAM_E_SAVE
00360  
00361          ; CPU detection code. Determine if this CPU is a 65C02 or 65816.
00362  
00363          ; Try to switch into emulation mode.
00364  008180  38                    SEC
00365  008181  FB                    XCE     ; This is a NOP on a 65C02.
00366  
00367          ; Try to switch into native mode.
00368  008182  18                    CLC
00369  008183  FB                    XCE     ; This is a NOP on a 65C02. C will be set on a 65816.
00370  
00371          ; X = 0 if the CPU is a 65C02.
00372  008184  A2 00                 LDX     #$00
00373  
00374          ; If carry is clear, the CPU is 65C02, not 65816.
00375  008186  90 01                 BCC     .skip_inx
00376  
00377          ; If the CPU is a 65816, carry will be set, and X will be 1.
00378  008188  E8                    INX
00379  
00380  .skip_inx:
00381  008189  FB                    XCE     ; Switch into emulation mode. This is a NOP on a 65C02.
00382  00818A  8E 10 7E              STX     RAM_CPU_TYPE
00383  
00384          ; Pull the prior value of A, pushed before the call to
00385          ; Continue_System_Init. If this was called from a physical
00386          ; RESET, $01 is pushed. Otherwise, whatever was in A is pushed.
00387  00818D  68                    PLA
00388  00818E  F0 16                 BEQ     .skip_shadow_vec_init
00389  
00390          ; a RESET has occurred, so initialize all the shadow vectors.
00391          ; Initialize all shadow vectors to point to an infinite loop.
00392          ; Done in two passes. This pass sets the LSB of the vector.
00393  008190  A9 1F                 lda     #<Infinite_Loop
00394  008192  A2 1C                 ldx     #$1C
00395  .lsb_loop:
00396  008194  9D E2 7E              sta     SHADOW_VECTOR_START-2,x
00397  008197  CA                    dex
00398  008198  CA                    dex
00399  008199  D0 F9                 BNE     .lsb_loop
00400  
00401          ; Finish initializing the shadow registers by writing the MSB.
00402  00819B  A9 81                 lda     #>Infinite_Loop
00403  00819D  A2 1C                 ldx     #$1C
00404  .msb_loop:
00405  00819F  9D E3 7E              sta     SHADOW_VECTOR_START-1,x
00406  0081A2  CA                    dex
00407  0081A3  CA                    dex
00408  0081A4  D0 F9                 BNE     .msb_loop
00409  
00410  .skip_shadow_vec_init:
00411          ; We're now in the debugging monitor.
00412  0081A6  A9 01                 LDA     #$01
00413  0081A8  8D 11 7E              STA     RAM_IN_MONITOR
00414  
00415          ; Store 0 in the location after RAM_IN_MONITOR. Not sure why.
00416  0081AB  3A                    dec
00417  0081AC  8D 12 7E              STA     RAM_IN_MONITOR+1
00418  
00419          ; Set a pointer to the default BRK handler when in native mode.
00420  0081AF  A9 32                 lda     #<BRK_816_Entry_Vector_Default
00421  0081B1  8D 74 7E              sta     BRK_816_ENTRY_VECTOR
00422  0081B4  A9 85                 lda     #>BRK_816_Entry_Vector_Default
00423  0081B6  8D 75 7E              STA     BRK_816_ENTRY_VECTOR+1
00424          
00425          ; Set a pointer to the default NMI handler when in native mode.
00426  0081B9  A9 3F                 LDA     #<NMI_816_Entry_Vector_Default
00427  0081BB  8D 76 7E              STA     NMI_816_ENTRY_VECTOR
00428  0081BE  A9 85                 LDA     #>NMI_816_Entry_Vector_Default
00429  0081C0  8D 77 7E              STA     NMI_816_ENTRY_VECTOR+1
00430  
00431          ; Set a pointer to the default IRQ entry vector.
00432  0081C3  A9 AF                 lda     #<IRQ_02_Entry_Vector_Default
00433  0081C5  8D 70 7E              sta     IRQ_02_ENTRY_VECTOR
00434  0081C8  A9 84                 lda     #>IRQ_02_Entry_Vector_Default
00435  0081CA  8D 71 7E              STA     IRQ_02_ENTRY_VECTOR+1
00436  
00437          ; Set a pointer to the default NMI entry vector.
00438  0081CD  A9 CF                 lda     #<NMI_02_Entry_Vector_Default
00439  0081CF  8D 72 7E              sta     NMI_02_ENTRY_VECTOR
00440  0081D2  A9 84                 lda     #>NMI_02_Entry_Vector_Default
00441  0081D4  8D 73 7E              STA     NMI_02_ENTRY_VECTOR+1
00442  
00443  0081D7  20 B1 85              jsr     Initialize_System_VIA
00444  0081DA  60                    rts
00445  
00446  ; Saves the first 5 bytes of zero-page memory, and syncs with the debugger,
00447  ; allowing it to control the device.
00448  ; Upon entry, the CPU will always be in emulation mode.
00449  Save_ZP_Sync_With_Debugger:
00450          ; Copy the first 5 bytes of ZP to the work area in RAM.
00451  0081DB  A2 04                 ldx     #$04
00452  .copy_loop:
00453  0081DD  BD 00 00              lda     \2DBG_VAR_00,x
00454  0081E0  9D 14 7E              sta     RAM_ZP_SAVE,x
00455  0081E3  CA                    dex
00456  0081E4  10 F7                 BPL     .copy_loop
00457  
00458  .begin_debugger_sync:
00459          ; Read the first snc char from the debugger.
00460  0081E6  20 06 86              JSR     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_RX
00461  
00462  .check_for_0x55:
00463          ; If the first sync char is not $55, restart the sync process.
00464  0081E9  C9 55                 cmp     #$55
00465  0081EB  D0 F9                 BNE     .begin_debugger_sync
00466  
00467          ; Read the second cync char from the debugger.
00468  0081ED  20 06 86              JSR     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_RX
00469  
00470          ; If the second sync char is not $AA, check for %55.
00471  0081F0  C9 AA                 CMP     #$AA
00472  0081F2  D0 F5                 BNE     .check_for_0x55
00473          
00474          ; Send a $CC to the debugger.
00475  0081F4  A9 CC                 lda     #$CC
00476  0081F6  20 2B 86              JSR     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_TX
00477  
00478          ; Read the command byte from the debugger.
00479  0081F9  20 06 86              JSR     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_RX
00480  
00481          ; See if the command is within the supported range. If not,
00482          ; restart the debugger sync sequence.
00483  0081FC  38                    sec
00484  0081FD  E9 00                 sbc     #$00
00485  0081FF  C9 0A                 cmp     #$0A
00486  008201  B0 E3                 BCS     .begin_debugger_sync
00487  
00488          ; Set up a simulated function call to jump to the handler
00489          ; for the selected debugger command. Multiple the command
00490          ; by two since each function pointer is two bytes.
00491  008203  0A                    asl
00492  008204  AA                    TAX
00493  
00494          ; Push the address-1 to return to once the command is complete.
00495          ; We'll return to .begin_debugger_sync:.
00496  008205  A9 81                 lda     #>{.begin_debugger_sync-1}
00497  008207  48                    pha
00498  008208  A9 E5                 lda     #<{.begin_debugger_sync-1}
00499  00820A  48                    PHA
00500  
00501          ; Push the jump table address and issue the RTS to call the handler.
00502  00820B  BD 15 82              lda     Cmd_Jump_Table+1,x
00503  00820E  48                    pha
00504  00820F  BD 14 82              lda     Cmd_Jump_Table,x
00505  008212  48                    pha
00506  008213  60                    rts
00507  
00508  ; Jump table for debugger commands.
00509  Cmd_Jump_Table:
00510          .WORD   Dbg_Cmd_0_Send_Zero         - 1
00511          .WORD   Dbg_Cmd_1_Seq_Test          - 1
00512          .WORD   Dbg_Cmd_2_Write_Mem         - 1
00513          .WORD   Dbg_Cmd_3_Read_Mem          - 1
00514          .WORD   Dbg_Cmd_4_Sys_Info          - 1
00515          .WORD   Dbg_Cmd_5_Exec              - 1
00516          .WORD   Dbg_Cmd_6_No_Op             - 1
00517          .WORD   Dbg_Cmd_7_No_Op             - 1
00518          .WORD   Dbg_Cmd_8_BRK               - 1
00519          .WORD   Dbg_Cmd_9_Read_Byte_and_BRK - 1
00520  
00521  ; Debugger command 0. Simply sends $00 to the debugger.
00522  Dbg_Cmd_0_Send_Zero:
00523  008228  A9 00                 LDA     #$00
00524  00822A  4C 2B 86              jmp     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_TX
00525  
00526  ; Debugger command 1: some kind of sequence test. Debugger sends a 16-bit
00527  ; count of the bytes to test. The debugger must then send an incrementing
00528  ; sequence of bytes, starting at $00 to the monitor. The monitor sends
00529  ; back the next expected byte. If the monitor receives a byte it does not
00530  ; expect, it enters an infinite loop.
00531  Dbg_Cmd_1_Seq_Test:
00532  
00533          ; DBG_VAR_02 is the next value in the sequence. Start with $00.
00534  00822D  A9 00                 lda     #$00
00535  00822F  8D 02 00              STA     \2DBG_VAR_02
00536  
00537         ; Read the LSB of the byte count.
00538  008232  20 06 86              JSR     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_RX
00539  008235  8D 00 00              sta     \2DBG_VAR_00
00540  
00541          ; Read the MSB of the byte count.
00542  008238  20 06 86              jsr     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_RX
00543  00823B  8D 01 00              STA     \2DBG_VAR_01
00544  
00545          ; If the byte count is 0, we're done.
00546  00823E  0D 00 00              ora     \2DBG_VAR_00
00547  008241  F0 26                 BEQ     .done
00548  
00549          ; Set up the count's MSB to be 1-based.
00550  008243  AD 00 00              LDA     \2DBG_VAR_00
00551  008246  F0 03                 beq     .read_next_byte
00552  008248  EE 01 00              INC     \2DBG_VAR_01
00553  
00554  .read_next_byte:
00555          ; Read the next byte in the sequence from the debugger.
00556  00824B  20 06 86              JSR     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_RX
00557  
00558          ; See if the received byte matches the next one in the sequence.
00559  00824E  CD 02 00              CMP     \2DBG_VAR_02
00560  008251  F0 05                 BEQ     .continue
00561  
00562          ; If the sequence is not correct, enter an infinite loop.
00563  .infinite_loop:
00564  008253  20 72 86              jsr     Do_Nothing_Subroutine_2
00565  008256  80 FB                 BRA     .infinite_loop
00566          
00567  .continue:
00568          ; Send the next byte in the sequence to the debugger.
00569  008258  1A                    inc
00570  008259  20 2B 86              JSR     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_TX
00571  
00572          ; Save the next byte in the sequence.
00573  00825C  EE 02 00              INC     \2DBG_VAR_02
00574  
00575          ; Decrement the byte count.
00576  00825F  CE 00 00              dec     \2DBG_VAR_00
00577  008262  D0 E7                 bne     .read_next_byte
00578  008264  CE 01 00              dec     \2DBG_VAR_01
00579  008267  D0 E2                 BNE     .read_next_byte
00580  
00581          ; All done with the command.
00582  008269  60            .done:  rts
00583  
00584  ; Debugger command 2: write memory. The debugger sends a 24-bit starting
00585  ; address, then a 16-bit count, and then the data to write. Memory writes
00586  ; to the first 5 bytes of memory are automatically redirected to the save
00587  ; area in work-RAM for these memory locations.
00588  Dbg_Cmd_2_Write_Mem:
00589  
00590          ; Read the 24-bit starting address, LSB-first.
00591  00826A  20 06 86              jsr     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_RX
00592  00826D  8D 00 00              sta     \2DBG_VAR_00	; 16-bit addr LSB
00593  008270  20 06 86              jsr     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_RX
00594  008273  8D 01 00              sta     \2DBG_VAR_01	; 16-bit addr MSB
00595  008276  20 06 86              jsr     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_RX
00596  008279  8D 02 00              STA     \2DBG_VAR_02	; bank
00597  
00598          ; Branch if bank is > $00.
00599  00827C  A9 00                 lda     #$00
00600  00827E  CD 02 00              cmp     \2DBG_VAR_02
00601  008281  90 1C                 BCC     .read_byte_count
00602  
00603          ; At this point, bank is $00. Branch if page (16-bit MSB) is > $80.
00604  008283  A9 80                 lda     #$80
00605  008285  CD 01 00              cmp     \2DBG_VAR_01
00606  008288  90 15                 BCC     .read_byte_count
00607  
00608          ; At this point, bank=0, page <= $80. Branch if addr LSB > $00.
00609  00828A  A9 00                 lda     #$00
00610  00828C  CD 00 00              cmp     \2DBG_VAR_00
00611  00828F  90 0E                 BCC     .read_byte_count
00612  
00613          ; At this point, bank=0, page <= $80, addr_LSB=0, which is the
00614          ; first byte of any page in RAM, plus the first page of FLASH,
00615          ; in bank 0. Now branch if bank <= 1, which is always the case,
00616          ; since bank is $00 at this point. Why are they doing all this?
00617  008291  A9 01                 lda     #$01
00618  008293  CD 02 00              cmp     \2DBG_VAR_02
00619  008296  B0 07                 BCS     .read_byte_count
00620  
00621          ; This code stores $01 in RAM_VAR_7E19, but this code is apparently
00622          ; never executed. This means RAM_VAR_7E19 will always be $00.
00623  008298  A9 01                 lda     #$01
00624  00829A  8D 19 7E              sta     RAM_VAR_7E19
00625  00829D  80 43                 BRA     .next_addr
00626  
00627  .read_byte_count:
00628          ; Read the 16-bit byte count from the debugger, LSB-first.
00629  00829F  20 06 86              JSR     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_RX
00630  0082A2  8D 03 00              sta     \2DBG_VAR_03
00631  0082A5  20 06 86              jsr     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_RX
00632  0082A8  8D 04 00              STA     \2DBG_VAR_04
00633  
00634          ; If the tranfer count is 0, cleanup and return.
00635  0082AB  0D 03 00              ora     \2DBG_VAR_03
00636  0082AE  F0 49                 BEQ     .cleanup
00637  
00638          ; Set the MSB of the transfer count to be 1-based.
00639  0082B0  A0 00                 ldy     #$00
00640  0082B2  AD 03 00              lda     \2DBG_VAR_03
00641  0082B5  F0 03                 beq     .transfer_byte
00642  0082B7  EE 04 00              INC     \2DBG_VAR_04
00643  
00644  .transfer_byte:
00645          ; If the address is not in the first bank and first page, then
00646          ; transfer the memory contents from the actual memory location.
00647  0082BA  AD 01 00              lda     \2DBG_VAR_01
00648  0082BD  0D 02 00              ora     \2DBG_VAR_02
00649  0082C0  D0 12                 BNE     .transfer_byte_from_real_addr
00650  
00651          ; Now see if the address is within the first five bytes of RAM.
00652          ; This address is used for debugger command parameters.
00653  0082C2  AD 00 00              lda     \2DBG_VAR_00
00654  0082C5  C9 05                 cmp     #$05
00655  0082C7  B0 0B                 BCS     .transfer_byte_from_real_addr
00656  
00657          ; The address is within the 5-byte debugger area in the zero-
00658          ; page. First, read the byte from the debugger to write.
00659  0082C9  A8                    tay
00660  0082CA  20 06 86              JSR     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_RX
00661  
00662          ; Now save the byte into the save area in work-RAM.
00663  0082CD  99 14 7E              STA     RAM_ZP_SAVE,y
00664  
00665          ; Move to the next byte to transfer.
00666  0082D0  A0 00                 ldy     #$00
00667  0082D2  F0 0E                 BEQ     .next_addr
00668  
00669  .transfer_byte_from_real_addr:
00670          ; Read the byte to write from the debugger.
00671  0082D4  20 06 86              JSR     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_RX
00672  
00673          ; See if we're running on a 65C02 or a 65816.
00674  0082D7  AE 10 7E              ldx     RAM_CPU_TYPE
00675  0082DA  D0 04                 BNE     .cpu_is_65816
00676  
00677          ; For the 65C02, ignore the bank, and only use the 16-bit addr.
00678  0082DC  91 00                 sta     (DBG_VAR_00),y
00679  0082DE  F0 02                 BEQ     .next_addr
00680  
00681  .cpu_is_65816:
00682          ; Use the ZP-indirect-long mode to write to the full 24-bit addr.
00683  0082E0  87 00                 STA     [0]
00684  
00685  .next_addr:
00686          ; Move to the next address.
00687  0082E2  EE 00 00              INC     \2DBG_VAR_00
00688  0082E5  D0 08                 bne     .dec_count
00689  0082E7  EE 01 00              inc     \2DBG_VAR_01
00690  0082EA  D0 03                 bne     .dec_count
00691  0082EC  EE 02 00              INC     \2DBG_VAR_02
00692  
00693  .dec_count:
00694          ; Decrement the transfer count, and see if we're done.
00695  0082EF  CE 03 00              DEC     \2DBG_VAR_03
00696  0082F2  D0 C6                 bne     .transfer_byte
00697  0082F4  CE 04 00              dec     \2DBG_VAR_04
00698  0082F7  D0 C1                 BNE     .transfer_byte
00699  
00700  .cleanup:
00701          ; Clear RAM_VAR_7E19 for some unknown reason. But it would never
00702          ; get set in the first place, so this code seems unnecessary.
00703  0082F9  AD 19 7E              LDA     RAM_VAR_7E19
00704  0082FC  F0 03                 beq     .done
00705  0082FE  9C 19 7E              STZ     RAM_VAR_7E19
00706  
00707  008301  60            .done:  rts
00708  
00709  ; Debugger command 3: read memory. The debugger sends a 24-bit starting
00710  ; address, then a 16-bit count. and then the monitor sends the request
00711  ; memory contents to the debugger. Memory reads to the first 5 bytes of
00712  ; memory are automatically redirected to the save area in work-RAM for
00713  ; these memory locations.
00714  Dbg_Cmd_3_Read_Mem:
00715          ; Read the 24-bit starting address, LSB-first.
00716  008302  20 06 86              jsr     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_RX
00717  008305  8D 00 00              sta     \2DBG_VAR_00	; 16-bit LSB
00718  008308  20 06 86              jsr     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_RX
00719  00830B  8D 01 00              sta     \2DBG_VAR_01	; Page
00720  00830E  20 06 86              jsr     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_RX
00721  008311  8D 02 00              STA     \2DBG_VAR_02	; Bank
00722  
00723          ; Read the 16-bit byte count, LSB-first.
00724  008314  20 06 86              jsr     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_RX
00725  008317  8D 03 00              sta     \2DBG_VAR_03	; Count LSB
00726  00831A  20 06 86              jsr     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_RX
00727  00831D  8D 04 00              STA     \2DBG_VAR_04	; Count MSB
00728  
00729          ; If the byte count is 0, then we're done.
00730  008320  0D 03 00              ora     \2DBG_VAR_03
00731  008323  F0 46                 BEQ     .done
00732  
00733          ; Set up the count MSB to be 1-based.
00734  008325  A0 00                 ldy     #$00
00735  008327  AD 03 00              lda     \2DBG_VAR_03
00736  00832A  F0 03                 beq     .transfer_byte
00737  00832C  EE 04 00              INC     \2DBG_VAR_04
00738  
00739  .transfer_byte:
00740          ; If the address is not in the first bank and first page, then
00741          ; transfer the memory contents from the actual memory location.
00742  00832F  AD 01 00              lda     \2DBG_VAR_01
00743  008332  0D 02 00              ora     \2DBG_VAR_02
00744  008335  D0 0F                 BNE     .transfer_byte_from_real_addr
00745  
00746          ; Now see if the address is within the first five bytes of RAM.
00747          ; This address is used for debugger command parameters.
00748  008337  AD 00 00              lda     \2DBG_VAR_00
00749  00833A  C9 05                 cmp     #$05
00750  00833C  B0 08                 BCS     .transfer_byte_from_real_addr
00751  
00752          ; The address is within the 5-byte debugger area in the zero-page,
00753          ; so send the contents of the save area in RAM to the debugger.
00754  00833E  A8                    tay
00755  00833F  B9 14 7E              LDA     RAM_ZP_SAVE,y
00756  
00757          ; Move to the next byte to transfer.
00758  008342  A0 00                 ldy     #$00
00759  008344  F0 0B                 BEQ     .next_addr
00760  
00761  .transfer_byte_from_real_addr:
00762          ; See if we're running on a 65C02 or a 65816.
00763  008346  AD 10 7E              lda     RAM_CPU_TYPE
00764  008349  D0 04                 BNE     .cpu_is_65816
00765  
00766          ; For the 65C02, ignore the bank, and only use the 16-bit addr.
00767  00834B  B1 00                 lda     (DBG_VAR_00),y
00768  00834D  80 02                 BRA     .next_addr
00769  
00770  .cpu_is_65816:
00771          ; Use the ZP-indirect-long mode to read from the full 24-bit addr.
00772  00834F  A7 00                 LDA     [0]
00773  
00774  .next_addr:
00775          ; Send the byte read from memory to the debugger.
00776  008351  20 2B 86              JSR     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_TX
00777  
00778          ; Move to the next address.
00779  008354  EE 00 00              inc     \2DBG_VAR_00
00780  008357  D0 08                 bne     .dec_count
00781  008359  EE 01 00              inc     \2DBG_VAR_01
00782  00835C  D0 03                 bne     .dec_count
00783  00835E  EE 02 00              INC     \2DBG_VAR_02
00784  
00785  .dec_count:
00786          ; Decrement the transfer count, and see if we're done.
00787  008361  CE 03 00              DEC     \2DBG_VAR_03
00788  008364  D0 C9                 bne     .transfer_byte
00789  008366  CE 04 00              dec     \2DBG_VAR_04
00790  008369  D0 C4                 BNE     .transfer_byte
00791  
00792  00836B  60            .done:  rts
00793  
00794  ; Debugger command 4. Get System Info.
00795  Dbg_Cmd_4_Sys_Info:
00796          ; Send $00:7E00 to the debugger, which is the start of the monitor
00797          ; work-RAM. This same address is also sent later, for some reason.
00798  00836C  A9 00                 lda     #<WORK_RAM_START
00799  00836E  20 2B 86              jsr     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_TX
00800  008371  A9 7E                 lda     #>WORK_RAM_START
00801  008373  20 2B 86              jsr     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_TX
00802  008376  A9 00                 LDA     #{WORK_RAM_START>>16}
00803  008378  20 2B 86              JSR     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_TX
00804  
00805          ; Auto-detected CPU type.
00806  00837B  AD 10 7E              lda     RAM_CPU_TYPE
00807  00837E  20 2B 86              JSR     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_TX
00808  
00809          ; Board ID.
00810  008381  A9 58                 lda     #BOARD_ID
00811  008383  20 2B 86              JSR     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_TX
00812  
00813          ; Send the work-RAM start address again. Not sure why, but this copy is
00814          ; the value that is displayed in the "Target Connection Information"
00815          ; screen on the debugger, so this copy is used, and not ignored.
00816  008386  A9 00                 lda     #<WORK_RAM_START
00817  008388  20 2B 86              jsr     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_TX
00818  00838B  A9 7E                 lda     #>WORK_RAM_START
00819  00838D  20 2B 86              jsr     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_TX
00820  008390  A9 00                 LDA     #{WORK_RAM_START>>16}
00821  008392  20 2B 86              jsr     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_TX
00822  
00823          ; Send the monitor code starting address.
00824  008395  A9 00                 lda     #<MONITOR_CODE_START
00825  008397  20 2B 86              jsr     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_TX
00826  00839A  A9 80                 lda     #>MONITOR_CODE_START
00827  00839C  20 2B 86              jsr     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_TX
00828  00839F  A9 00                 lda     #{MONITOR_CODE_START>>16}
00829  0083A1  20 2B 86              JSR     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_TX
00830  
00831          ; Shadow vector start (24-bit address, LSB-first).
00832  0083A4  A9 E4                 lda     #<SHADOW_VECTOR_START
00833  0083A6  20 2B 86              jsr     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_TX
00834  0083A9  A9 7E                 LDA     #>SHADOW_VECTOR_START
00835  0083AB  20 2B 86              JSR     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_TX
00836  0083AE  A9 00                 lda     #{SHADOW_VECTOR_START>>16}
00837  0083B0  20 2B 86              JSR     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_TX
00838  
00839          ; Shadow vector end address + 1.
00840  0083B3  A9 00                 lda     #<{SHADOW_VECTOR_START + SHADOW_VECTOR_SIZE}
00841  0083B5  20 2B 86              jsr     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_TX
00842  0083B8  A9 7F                 lda     #>{SHADOW_VECTOR_START + SHADOW_VECTOR_SIZE}
00843  0083BA  20 2B 86              jsr     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_TX
00844  0083BD  A9 00                 LDA     #{{SHADOW_VECTOR_START + SHADOW_VECTOR_SIZE}>>16}
00845  0083BF  20 2B 86              jsr     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_TX
00846  
00847          ; Send the hardware vector address.
00848  0083C2  A9 E4                 lda     #<CPU_VECTOR_START
00849  0083C4  20 2B 86              jsr     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_TX
00850  0083C7  A9 FF                 lda     #>CPU_VECTOR_START
00851  0083C9  20 2B 86              jsr     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_TX
00852  0083CC  A9 00                 LDA     #{CPU_VECTOR_START>>16}
00853  0083CE  20 2B 86              jsr     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_TX
00854  
00855          ; Send the hardware base IO address.
00856  0083D1  A9 00                 lda     #<HW_IO_START
00857  0083D3  20 2B 86              jsr     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_TX
00858  0083D6  A9 7F                 lda     #>HW_IO_START
00859  0083D8  20 2B 86              jsr     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_TX
00860  0083DB  A9 00                 LDA     #{HW_IO_START>>16}
00861  0083DD  20 2B 86              jsr     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_TX
00862  
00863          ; Not sure, but assume this is the last byte of the hardware IO area.
00864  0083E0  A9 FF                 lda     #<{HW_IO_START + HW_IO_SIZE - 1}
00865  0083E2  20 2B 86              jsr     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_TX
00866  0083E5  A9 7F                 lda     #>{HW_IO_START + HW_IO_SIZE - 1}
00867  0083E7  20 2B 86              jsr     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_TX
00868  0083EA  A9 00                 LDA     #{{HW_IO_START + HW_IO_SIZE - 1}>>16}
00869  0083EC  20 2B 86              jsr     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_TX
00870  
00871          ; Send the hardware breakpoint address.
00872  0083EF  A9 FF                 lda     #<HW_BRK_ADDR
00873  0083F1  20 2B 86              jsr     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_TX
00874  0083F4  A9 FF                 lda     #>HW_BRK_ADDR
00875  0083F6  20 2B 86              jsr     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_TX
00876  0083F9  A9 FF                 lda     #{HW_BRK_ADDR>>16}
00877  0083FB  4C 2B 86              jmp     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_TX
00878  
00879  ; Debugger command 5. Restore the CPU context and execute from the saved context.
00880  Dbg_Cmd_5_Exec:
00881  
00882          ; Restore the user's state of the VIA's PCR register.
00883  0083FE  20 6B 86              JSR     Restore_VIA_PCR_State
00884  
00885          ; Restore the 5 zero-page variables from the copies in work-RAM.
00886  008401  A2 04                 LDX     #$04
00887  .copy_zp_var:
00888  008403  BD 14 7E              lda     RAM_ZP_SAVE,x
00889  008406  9D 00 00              sta     \2DBG_VAR_00,x
00890  008409  CA                    dex
00891  00840A  10 F7                 BPL     .copy_zp_var
00892  
00893          ; See if the CPU was running in emulation mode.
00894  00840C  AD 0D 7E              lda     RAM_E_SAVE
00895  00840F  F0 2D                 BEQ     .was_in_native_mode
00896  
00897          ; The CPU was in emulation mode. Restore the CPU context. Start off
00898          ; by restoring the stack and the index registers.
00899  008411  AE 0A 7E              ldx     RAM_SP_SAVE
00900  008414  9A                    txs
00901  008415  AE 02 7E              ldx     RAM_X_SAVE
00902  008418  AC 04 7E              LDY     RAM_Y_SAVE
00903  
00904          ; See what CPU type we're running.
00905  00841B  AD 10 7E              lda     RAM_CPU_TYPE
00906  00841E  D0 09                 BNE     .cpu_is_65816
00907  
00908          ; CPU is 65C02. The below code pushes the saved direct-page contents
00909          ; onto the stack. Not sure why, since in emulation mode, these will
00910          ; always both be 0.
00911  008420  AD 09 7E              lda     RAM_DP_SAVE+1
00912  008423  48                    pha
00913  008424  AD 08 7E              lda     RAM_DP_SAVE
00914  008427  48                    PHA
00915  
00916          ; Pull the direct-page register from the stack. But, since this is
00917          ; running on a 65C02, this will actually be a no-op. Seems like the
00918          ; stack will have two extra bytes on it (the direct page). Why?!?
00919  008428  2B                    PLD
00920  
00921  .cpu_is_65816:
00922          ; Set up a simulated ISR on the stack.
00923  008429  AD 07 7E              LDA     RAM_PC_SAVE+1
00924  00842C  48                    pha
00925  00842D  AD 06 7E              lda     RAM_PC_SAVE
00926  008430  48                    pha
00927  008431  AD 0C 7E              lda     RAM_P_SAVE
00928  008434  48                    PHA
00929  
00930          ; We're no longer in the ROM monitor since we're going to execute user code.
00931  008435  A9 00                 lda     #$00
00932  008437  8D 11 7E              STA     RAM_IN_MONITOR
00933  
00934          ; Restore the A register.
00935  00843A  AD 00 7E              LDA     RAM_A_SAVE
00936  
00937          ; Perform an RTI, restoring the CPU context as it was.
00938  00843D  40                    rti
00939  
00940  .was_in_native_mode:
00941          ; Set the CPU to native mode.
00942  00843E  18                    CLC
00943  00843F  FB                    XCE
00944  
00945          ; Set XY to 16-bit mode, and A to 8-bit mode.
00946  008440  E2 20                 SEP     #$20
00947  008442  C2 10                 REP     #$10
00948  
00949          ; Restore the 16-bit stack and Direct Page registers.
00950  008444  AE 0A 7E              ldx     RAM_SP_SAVE
00951  008447  9A                    txs
00952  008448  AE 08 7E              ldx     RAM_DP_SAVE
00953  00844B  DA                    phx
00954  00844C  2B                    PLD
00955  
00956          ; Set up a simulated ISR on the stack.
00957  00844D  AD 0E 7E              lda     RAM_PB_SAVE
00958  008450  48                    pha
00959  008451  AE 06 7E              ldx     RAM_PC_SAVE
00960  008454  DA                    phx
00961  008455  AD 0C 7E              lda     RAM_P_SAVE
00962  008458  48                    pha
00963  008459  AE 02 7E              ldx     RAM_X_SAVE
00964  00845C  AC 04 7E              LDY     RAM_Y_SAVE
00965  
00966          ; We're no longer in the ROM monitor since we're going to execute user code.
00967  00845F  A9 00                 lda     #$00
00968  008461  8D 11 7E              STA     RAM_IN_MONITOR
00969  
00970          ; Restore the data bank register.
00971  008464  AD 0F 7E              lda     RAM_DB_SAVE
00972  008467  48                    pha
00973  008468  AB                    PLB
00974  
00975          ; Set A to 16-bit mode.
00976  008469  C2 20                 REP     #$20
00977  
00978          ; Restore the 16-bit A register.
00979  00846B  AF 00 7E 00           LDA     \3RAM_A_SAVE
00980  
00981          ; Perform an RTI, restoring the CPU context as it was.
00982  00846F  40                    RTI
00983  
00984  ; Debugger commands 6 and 7. They do nothing.
00985  Dbg_Cmd_6_No_Op:
00986  Dbg_Cmd_7_No_Op:
00987  
00988          ; Return, making this debug command a no-op.
00989  008470  60                    rts
00990  
00991          ; This code is apparently never called.
00992  008471  4C 2B 86              jmp     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_TX
00993  008474  A9 25                 lda     #$25
00994  008476  80 20                 bra     Dbg_Cmd_8_Done
00995  008478  2B                    PLD
00996  008479  86 A9                 stx     $A9
00997  00847B  80 00                 bra     .branch
00998  .branch:
00999  00847D  20 2B 86              JSR     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_TX
01000          ; See notes for Dbg_Cmd_8_BRK about 8-bit LDA and BRK vs. 16-bit LDA.
01001  008480  A9 00                 LDA     #$00
01002          .DB     $00 ; Single-byte BRK instruction.
01003  008483  4C 2B 86              jmp     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_TX
01004  
01005  ; Debugger command 8. Executes a BRK instruction, causing the monitor to send
01006  ; a $02 to the debugger, as it normally does when a BRK is executed. Not sure why
01007  ; this debugger command exists, or how/if it is useful at all.
01008  Dbg_Cmd_8_BRK:
01009  008486  20 97 84              jsr     .clear_carry
01010  008489  90 06                 BCC     .on_carry_clear
01011  
01012          ; The following code is apparently never executed. See notes below
01013          ; regarding an 8-bit immediate LDA and BRK vs. a 16-bit immediate LDA.
01014  00848B  A9 01                 LDA     #$01
01015          .DB     $00 ; Single-byte BRK instruction.
01016  00848E  4C 2B 86              jmp     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_TX
01017  
01018  .on_carry_clear:
01019  
01020          ; Perform an 8-bit immediate load, and generate a BRK. The BRK in this
01021          ; case is only a single byte, instead of two bytes which is typical.
01022          ; This could also be interpreted as a 16-bit immediate load of $0000,
01023          ; but since the CPU is always in emulation mode when this code is
01024          ; executed, it is clearer to write it as an 8-bit load and a BRK.
01025  008491  A9 00                 LDA     #$00
01026          .DB     $00 ; Single-byte BRK instruction.
01027  
01028          ; This is not executed because of the BRK above.
01029  008494  4C 2B 86              jmp     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_TX
01030  
01031  .clear_carry:
01032  008497  18                    CLC
01033  
01034  Dbg_Cmd_8_Done:
01035  008498  60                    RTS
01036  
01037  ; Debugger command 9. Reads a byte from the debugger, and then executes a BRK
01038  ; instruction, which then sends a $02 to the debugger. Not sure why this
01039  ;debugger command exists, or how/if it is useful at all.
01040  Dbg_Cmd_9_Read_Byte_and_BRK:
01041          ; Read a data byte from the debugger.
01042  008499  20 06 86              JSR     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_RX
01043  
01044  00849C  20 AD 84              jsr     .clear_carry
01045  00849F  90 06                 BCC     .on_carry_clear
01046

01048          ; regarding an 8-bit immediate LDA and BRK vs. a 16-bit immediate LDA.
01049  0084A1  A9 01                 LDA     #$01
01050          .DB     $00 ; Single-byte BRK instruction.
01051  0084A4  4C 2B 86              jmp     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_TX
01052  
01053  .on_carry_clear:
01054          ; The following code is apparently never executed. See DBG_CMD_8_BRK
01055          ; regarding an 8-bit immediate LDA and BRK vs. a 16-bit immediate LDA.
01056  0084A7  A9 00                 LDA     #$00
01057          .DB     $00 ; Single-byte BRK instruction.
01058  
01059          ; This is not executed because of the BRK above.
01060  0084AA  4C 2B 86              jmp     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_TX

01062  .clear_carry:
01063  0084AD  18                    CLC
01064  0084AE  60                    rts
01065  
01066  ; The default handler for IRQ when in '02 emulation mode.
01067  ; At this point, we are in emulation mode, so A and XY are in 8-bit mode.
01068  IRQ_02_Entry_Vector_Default:
01069  0084AF  48                    PHA     ; Save the LSB of A on the stack.
01070  
01071          ; We're now executing the ROM monitor code.
01072  0084B0  A9 01                 lda     #$01
01073  0084B2  8F 11 7E 00           STA     \3RAM_IN_MONITOR
01074  0084B6  DA                    PHX     ; Save X on the stack.
01075  
01076          ; Get the pushed P (status reg). This includes the B flag which
01077          ; was pushed. We're in '02 mode, so we know the stack is at $100.
01078  0084B7  BA                    tsx
01079  0084B8  BD 03 01              lda     $103,x
01080  0084BB  FA                    PLX
01081  
01082          ; See if the pushed copy of B is set, indicating a BRK vs IRQ.
01083  0084BC  29 10                 and     #$10
01084  0084BE  D0 0A                 BNE     .on_BRK
01085  
01086          ; An IRQ was received. Clean up the stack and call the user's
01087          ; IRQ vector through the shadow vector at $7EFE.
01088  0084C0  A9 00                 lda     #$00
01089  0084C2  8F 11 7E 00           STA     \3RAM_IN_MONITOR	; No longer in ROM monitor code.
01090  
01091  0084C6  68                    pla
01092  0084C7  6C FE 7E              jmp     (SHADOW_VEC_IRQ_02)
01093  
01094  ; Called when a BRK instruction is executed.
01095  .on_BRK:
01096          ; Set RAM_ENTER_MONITOR_REASON to 2, indicating a BRK was executed.
01097  0084CA  A9 02                 LDA     #$02
01098  0084CC  4C E2 84              jmp     Save_Context_Enter_Monitor_02_Mode
01099  
01100  ; The default handler for NMI when in '02 emulation mode.
01101  NMI_02_Entry_Vector_Default:
01102  0084CF  48                    PHA     ; Save the LSB of A on the stack.
01103  
01104          ; See if we were running monitor code or user code.
01105  0084D0  AF 11 7E 00           LDA     \3RAM_IN_MONITOR
01106  0084D4  D0 0A                 BNE     .was_running_monitor_code
01107  
01108          ; We were running user code, but now we're in the monitor.
01109  0084D6  A9 01                 lda     #$01
01110  0084D8  8F 11 7E 00           STA     \3RAM_IN_MONITOR
01111  
01112          ; Set RAM_ENTER_MONITOR_REASON to 7, indicating an NMI was generated.
01113  0084DC  A9 07                 lda     #$07
01114  0084DE  80 02                 BRA     Save_Context_Enter_Monitor_02_Mode
01115          
01116  .was_running_monitor_code:
01117          ; An NMI ocurred while running the monitor code. Ignore it by
01118          ; restoring the context and returning from the interrupt.
01119  0084E0  68                    pla
01120  0084E1  40                    rti
01121  
01122  ; Called while in '02 emulation mode to save the CPU context and
01123  ; then enter the ROM monitor.
01124  ;
01125  ; On entry, A must contain the reason the monitor will be entered.
01126  Save_Context_Enter_Monitor_02_Mode:
01127  
01128          ; Enter native mode.
01129  0084E2  80 3D                 BRA     .enter_native_mode
01130  
01131          ; The above is not a subroutine call, so it does not return.
01132          ; I don't think the following code is ever executed. Instead,
01133          ; the BRA above switches the CPU into native mode, and then
01134          ; the native-mode routine is called to save the CPU context.
01135  
01136          ; Save the reason we're entering the monitor into work-RAM.
01137  0084E4  8D 13 7E              STA     RAM_ENTER_MONITOR_REASON
01138  
01139          ; Save the 8-bit CPU context into work-RAM.
01140  0084E7  68                    pla
01141  0084E8  8D 00 7E              sta     RAM_A_SAVE
01142  0084EB  8E 02 7E              stx     RAM_X_SAVE
01143  0084EE  8C 04 7E              sty     RAM_Y_SAVE
01144  0084F1  68                    pla
01145  0084F2  8D 0C 7E              sta     RAM_P_SAVE
01146  0084F5  68                    pla
01147  0084F6  8D 06 7E              sta     RAM_PC_SAVE
01148  0084F9  68                    pla
01149  0084FA  8D 07 7E              STA     RAM_PC_SAVE+1
01150  
01151          ; We were in 6502 mode, so save 0 to the bank registers and
01152          ; the high bytes of the 16-bit registers.
01153  0084FD  9C 0E 7E              stz     RAM_PB_SAVE
01154  008500  9C 0F 7E              stz     RAM_DB_SAVE
01155  008503  9C 08 7E              stz     RAM_DP_SAVE
01156  008506  9C 09 7E              stz     RAM_DP_SAVE+1
01157  008509  9C 01 7E              stz     RAM_A_SAVE+1
01158  00850C  9C 03 7E              stz     RAM_X_SAVE+1
01159  00850F  9C 05 7E              STZ     RAM_Y_SAVE+1
01160  
01161          ; Save the LSB (8-bits) of the stack to work-RAM.
01162  008512  BA                    tsx
01163  008513  8E 0A 7E              STX     RAM_SP_SAVE
01164  
01165          ; We know we're in emulation mode, so save "1" to the high-byte
01166          ; of the stack pointer and the E(mulation) flag save area.
01167  008516  A9 01                 lda     #$01
01168  008518  8D 0B 7E              sta     RAM_SP_SAVE+1
01169  00851B  8D 0D 7E              STA     RAM_E_SAVE
01170  
01171          ; Per the comments above, I don't think this is ever actually
01172          ; called from here. Another reason is that the subroutine expects
01173          ; the CPU to be in emulation mode, and if this code were to be
01174          ; executed, it would be in we're in native mode now.
01175  00851E  4C A5 85              JMP     Send_Enter_Reason_and_Sync_With_Debugger
01176  
01177  .enter_native_mode:
01178          ; Switch to native mode.
01179  008521  18                    CLC
01180  008522  FB                    XCE
01181  
01182          ; Set XY and A to 8-bit mode.
01183  008523  E2 30                 SEP     #$30
01184  
01185          ; Save the reason we're entering the monitor into work-RAM.
01186  008525  8F 13 7E 00           STA     \3RAM_ENTER_MONITOR_REASON
01187  
01188          ; We were previously in emulation mode, so indicate this.
01189  008529  A9 01                 LDA     #$1
01190  00852B  8F 0D 7E 00           STA     \3RAM_E_SAVE
01191  
01192          ; Save the CPU context and enter the ROM monitor.
01193  00852F  4C 60 85              JMP     Save_Context_Enter_Monitor
01194  
01195  ; Unless the user overrides the default vector, then this is called
01196  ; when a BRK instruction is executed while in 816 native mode.
01197  BRK_816_Entry_Vector_Default:
01198          ; Set the A register to 8-bit mode and push the low part of it.
01199  008532  E2 20                 SEP     #$20
01200  008534  48                    PHA
01201  
01202          ; We're now running monitor code.
01203  008535  A9 01                 lda     #$01
01204  008537  8F 11 7E 00           STA     \3RAM_IN_MONITOR
01205  
01206          ; Set RAM_ENTER_MONITOR_REASON to 2, indicating a BRK was executed.
01207  00853B  A9 02                 lda     #$02
01208  00853D  80 15                 BRA     Save_Context_Enter_Monitor_816_Mode_With_Reason
01209  
01210  ; Unless the user overrides the default vector, then this is called
01211  ; upon an NMIA while the CPU is in 816 native mode.
01212  NMI_816_Entry_Vector_Default:
01213          ; Set the A register to 8-bit mode and push the low part of it.
01214  00853F  E2 20                 SEP     #$20
01215  008541  48                    PHA
01216  
01217          ; See if we were running monitor code when the NMI ocurred.
01218  008542  AF 11 7E 00           LDA     \3RAM_IN_MONITOR
01219  008546  D0 0A                 BNE     .was_running_monitor_code
01220  
01221          ; We're now running monitor code.
01222  008548  A9 01                 lda     #$01
01223  00854A  8F 11 7E 00           STA     \3RAM_IN_MONITOR
01224  
01225          ; Set RAM_ENTER_MONITOR_REASON to 7, indicating an NMI was generated.
01226  00854E  A9 07                 lda     #$07
01227  008550  80 02                 BRA     Save_Context_Enter_Monitor_816_Mode_With_Reason
01228  
01229  .was_running_monitor_code:
01230          ; An NMI ocurred while running the monitor code. Ignore it by
01231          ; restoring the context and returning from the interrupt.
01232  008552  68                    pla
01233  008553  40                    rti
01234  
01235  ; Called while in 816 native mode to save the CPU context and
01236  ; then enter the ROM monitor.
01237  Save_Context_Enter_Monitor_816_Mode_With_Reason:
01238  008554  E2 20                 SEP     #$20    ; Set the A register to 8-bit mode.
01239  
01240          ; Save the reason we're entering the monitor into work-RAM.
01241  008556  8F 13 7E 00           STA     \3RAM_ENTER_MONITOR_REASON
01242  
01243          ; We were previously in 816 native mode, so indicate this.
01244  00855A  A9 00                 lda     #$00
01245  00855C  8F 0D 7E 00           STA     \3RAM_E_SAVE
01246  
01247  ; Saves the CPU context and enters the ROM monitor, syncing with the debugger.
01248  ; This code is ultimately used by the BRK and NMI handlers in both native and
01249  ; emulation mode (after switching to native mode).
01250  ;
01251  ; Upon entry, the CPU must be in native 816 mode, with A set to 8-bit mode,
01252  ; with the low 8-bits of A already pushed to the stack.
01253  Save_Context_Enter_Monitor:
01254          ; Save the LSB of A into work-RAM.
01255  008560  68                    PLA
01256  008561  8F 00 7E 00           STA     \3RAM_A_SAVE
01257  
01258          ; Save the MSB of A into work-RAM.
01259  008565  EB                    XBA
01260  008566  8F 01 7E 00           STA     \3RAM_A_SAVE+1
01261  
01262          ; Save the data bank into work-RAM.
01263  00856A  8B                    PHB
01264  00856B  68                    pla
01265  00856C  8F 0F 7E 00           STA     \3RAM_DB_SAVE
01266  
01267          ; Switch to data bank 0.
01268  008570  A9 00                 lda     #$00
01269  008572  48                    pha
01270  008573  AB                    PLB
01271  
01272          ; Save 0 into the program bank save area in work-RAM. This value will
01273          ; remain if the CPU was in emulation mode, but it will be overwritten
01274          ; with the correct value later if the CPU was in native mode.
01275  008574  8F 0E 7E 00           STA     \3RAM_PB_SAVE
01276  
01277          ; Save the CPU status register to the area in work-RAM.
01278  008578  68                    pla
01279  008579  8F 0C 7E 00           STA     \3RAM_P_SAVE
01280  
01281          ; Set 16-bit A and XY registers.
01282  00857D  C2 30                 REP     #$30
01283  
01284          ; Save the direct-page register to the save area in work-RAM.
01285  00857F  7B                    TDC
01286  008580  8F 08 7E 00           STA     \3RAM_DP_SAVE
01287  
01288          ; Set the direct-page register to page 0.
01289  008584  A9 00 00              lda     \2#$00
01290  008587  5B                    TCD
01291  
01292          ; Save the X and Y registers (all 16-bits each) to work-RAM.
01293  008588  8E 02 7E              stx     RAM_X_SAVE
01294  00858B  8C 04 7E              STY     RAM_Y_SAVE
01295  
01296          ; Pull the 16-bit PC and save it to work RAM.
01297  00858E  68                    pla
01298  00858F  8D 06 7E              STA     RAM_PC_SAVE
01299  
01300          ; Set A to 8-bit mode.
01301  008592  E2 20                 SEP     #$20
01302  
01303          ; See if the CPU was in '02 '816 mode when it was interrupted.
01304  008594  AD 0D 7E              LDA     RAM_E_SAVE
01305  008597  D0 04                 BNE     .was_in_emulation_mode
01306  
01307          ; The CPU was in native mode. Pull the program bank and save it.
01308  008599  68                    pla
01309  00859A  8D 0E 7E              STA     RAM_PB_SAVE
01310  
01311  .was_in_emulation_mode:
01312          ; Save all 16-bits of the stack pointer. If the CPU was in emulation
01313          ; mode, the MSB will be saved as "1".
01314  00859D  BA                    tsx
01315  00859E  8E 0A 7E              STX     RAM_SP_SAVE
01316  
01317          ; Set 8-bit XY registers. At this point, A and XY are both 8-bit.
01318  0085A1  E2 10                 SEP     #$10
01319  
01320          ; The user's CPU context is now fully saved into work-RAM. Switch
01321          ; back into emulation mode.
01322  0085A3  38                    SEC
01323  0085A4  FB                    XCE
01324  
01325  ; Sends the reason the monitor (debugger) was entered, and then syncs
01326  ; with the debugger, allowing the debugger to control the device.
01327  Send_Enter_Reason_and_Sync_With_Debugger:
01328  
01329          ; Save the state of the system VIA's PCR so it can be restored later.
01330  0085A5  20 64 86              JSR     Save_VIA_PCR_State
01331  
01332          ; Send the reason we entered the monitor to the debugger.
01333  0085A8  AD 13 7E              LDA     RAM_ENTER_MONITOR_REASON
01334  0085AB  20 2B 86              JSR     Sys_VIA_USB_Char_TX
01335  
01336          ; Save the first five zero-page values, and sync with debugger.
01337  0085AE  4C DB 81              JMP     Save_ZP_Sync_With_Debugger
01338  
01339  ; Called in emulation mode upon system reset.
01340  ; Initializes the system VIA (the USB debugger), and syncs with the USB chip.
01341  Initialize_System_VIA:
01342  
01343          ; Disable PB7, shift register, timer T1 interrupt.
01344  0085B1  A9 00                 lda     #$00
01345  0085B3  8D EB 7F              STA     SYSTEM_VIA_ACR
01346  
01347          ; Cx1/Cx2 as inputs with negative active edge, for both ports. These
01348          ; aren't used for the system VIA debugging interface, but the Cx2
01349          ; lines are connected to the FLASH, and they select the bank. Setting
01350          ; them as inputs allows the pullups to automatically select the bank
01351          ; which contains the factory-programmed FLASH bank with the monitor.
01352  0085B6  A9 00                 lda     #$00
01353  0085B8  8D EC 7F              STA     SYSTEM_VIA_PCR
01354  
01355          ; Save the PCR in work-RAM so it can be restored later.
01356  0085BB  8D 1C 7E              STA     RAM_PCR_SAVE
01357  
01358          ; Preset port B output for $18 (TUSB_RDB and PB4-not-connected high).
01359  0085BE  A9 18                 lda     #$18
01360  0085C0  8D E0 7F              STA     SYSTEM_VIA_IOB
01361  
01362          ; Set PB2 (TUSB_WR), PB3 (TUSB_RDB), and PB4 (N.C.) as outputs. This
01363          ; has the effect of writing $FF to the USB FIFO when the RESET button
01364          ; is pressed. When RESET is pressed, it causes the system VIA to output
01365          ; high on TUSB_WR, then when this write sets TUSB_WR low, the high-to-
01366          ; low transition on TUSB_WR triggers a write to the USB FIFO. At this
01367          ; point, port A (the USB FIFO data lines) are not being driven, and
01368          ; either float high, or are pulled high internally, because this
01369          ; triggers a write of $FF to the USB FIFO.
01370  0085C3  A9 1C                 lda     #$1C
01371  0085C5  8D E2 7F              STA     SYSTEM_VIA_DDRB
01372  
01373          ; Save DDRB in work-RAM. Not sure why, since it is never used again.
01374  0085C8  8D 1D 7E              STA     RAM_DDRB_SAVE
01375  
01376          ; Set all IO on port A to inputs.
01377  0085CB  A9 00                 LDA     #$00
01378  0085CD  8D E3 7F              STA     SYSTEM_VIA_DDRA
01379  
01380          ; Save DDRA in work-RAM. Not sure why, since it is never used again.
01381  0085D0  8D 1E 7E              STA     RAM_DDRA_SAVE
01382  
01383          ; Read port B (USB status and control lines) and save it on the stack.
01384  0085D3  AD E0 7F              lda     SYSTEM_VIA_IOB
01385  0085D6  48                    PHA
01386  
01387          ; Mask out bit 4, which is not connected.
01388  0085D7  29 EF                 AND     #$EF
01389  
01390          ; Write the result back. Not sure why since only bit 4 changes, and
01391          ; it is not connected (according to schematic rev. C, Dec. 15, 2020).
01392  0085D9  8D E0 7F              STA     SYSTEM_VIA_IOB
01393  
01394          ; Delay for $5D*256 loop cycles.
01395  0085DC  A2 5D                 LDX     #$5D
01396  0085DE  20 59 86              JSR     Delay_Loop
01397  
01398          ; Pull the original port B value, and write it back to the port.
01399  0085E1  68                    PLA
01400  0085E2  8D E0 7F              STA     SYSTEM_VIA_IOB
01401  
01402          ; Wait until PB5 (TUSB_PWRENB) goes low, indicating it's powered up.
01403  0085E5  A9 20                 lda     #$20
01404  0085E7  2C E0 7F      .loop:  bit     SYSTEM_VIA_IOB
01405  0085EA  D0 FB                 BNE     .loop
01406  
01407          ; If PB6 (not connected) is 0, then make a no-op call. Why?!?
01408  0085EC  AD E0 7F              LDA     SYSTEM_VIA_IOB
01409  0085EF  29 40                 and     #$40
01410  0085F1  F0 65                 BEQ     Do_Nothing_Subroutine_1
01411  
01412          ; All done.
01413  0085F3  60                    RTS
01414  
01415  ; Returns 1 in A if there is data available to be read, 0 if not.
01416  Is_VIA_USB_RX_Data_Avail:
01417  
01418          ; Set all bits on port A to inputs.
01419  0085F4  A9 00                 LDA     #$00
01420  0085F6  8D E3 7F              STA     SYSTEM_VIA_DDRA
01421  
01422          ; See if PB1 (TUSB_RXFB) is high.
01423  0085F9  A9 02                 LDA     #$02
01424  0085FB  2C E0 7F              bit     SYSTEM_VIA_IOB
01425  0085FE  D0 03                 bne     .not_zero
01426  
01427          ; It is low, meaning there is data available to read.
01428  008600  A9 01                 LDA     #$01
01429  008602  60                    RTS
01430  
01431  .not_zero:
01432          ; It is high, meaning there is no data available to read.
01433  008603  A9 00                 LDA     #$00
01434  008605  60                    RTS
01435  
01436  ; Waits for a byte to be ready on the USB FIFO and then reads it, returning
01437  ; the value read in the A register.
01438  Sys_VIA_USB_Char_RX:
01439          ; Set all bits on port A to inputs.
01440  008606  A9 00                 lda     #$00
01441  008608  8D E3 7F              STA     SYSTEM_VIA_DDRA
01442  
01443          ; Set up to test PB1 (TUSB_RXFB).
01444  00860B  A9 02                 LDA     #$02
01445  
01446          ; Wait for PB1 (TUSB_RXFB) to be low. This indicates data can be
01447          ; read from the FIFO by strobing PB3 low then high again.
01448  .wait_for_rxfb_low:
01449  00860D  2C E0 7F              bit     SYSTEM_VIA_IOB
01450  008610  D0 FB                 BNE     .wait_for_rxfb_low
01451  
01452          ; Perform a read-modify-write on port B, clearing PB3 (TUSB_RDB).
01453          ; This triggers the FIFO to drive the received byte on port A.
01454  008612  AD E0 7F              lda     SYSTEM_VIA_IOB
01455  008615  09 08                 ora     #$08    ; Save a copy of port B with PB3 set high.
01456  008617  AA                    tax     ; This will be used later.
01457  008618  29 F7                 and     #$F7
01458  00861A  8D E0 7F              STA     SYSTEM_VIA_IOB
01459  
01460          ; Wait for the FIFO to drive the data and the lines to settle
01461          ; (between 20ns and 50ns, according to the datasheet).
01462  00861D  EA                    nop
01463  00861E  EA                    nop
01464  00861F  EA                    nop
01465  008620  EA                    NOP
01466  
01467          ; Read the data byte from the FIFO on port A.
01468  008621  AD E1 7F              LDA     SYSTEM_VIA_IOA
01469  
01470          ; Restore the original value of port B, while setting PB3 high again.
01471  008624  8E E0 7F              stx     SYSTEM_VIA_IOB
01472  
01473          ; We're done. The byte read is in A.
01474  008627  60                    RTS
01475  
01476          ; Apparently unused code.
01477  008628  A9 EE                 lda     #$EE
01478  00862A  60                    rts
01479  
01480  ; Sends the byte stored in A to the debugger, waiting until it can be sent.
01481  Sys_VIA_USB_Char_TX:
01482  
01483          ; Set all bits on port A to inputs.
01484  00862B  A2 00                 ldx     #$00
01485  00862D  8E E3 7F              STX     SYSTEM_VIA_DDRA
01486  
01487          ; Write register A to port A. This has no effect on the actual
01488          ; output pin until port A is set as an output.
01489  008630  8D E1 7F              STA     SYSTEM_VIA_IOA
01490  
01491          ; Set up register A to test port B, bit 0 (TUSB_TXEB).
01492  008633  A9 01                 LDA     #$01
01493  
01494          ; Wait for PB0 (TUSB_TXEB) to be low. This indicates data can be
01495          ; written to the FIFO by strobing PB2 (TUSB_WR) high then low.
01496  .wait_for_txeb_low:
01497  008635  2C E0 7F              bit     SYSTEM_VIA_IOB
01498  008638  D0 FB                 BNE     .wait_for_txeb_low
01499  
01500          ; Perform a read-modify-write on port B, setting bit 2 (TUSB_WR).
01501          ; Save the original value in X temporarily.
01502  00863A  AD E0 7F              lda     SYSTEM_VIA_IOB
01503  00863D  29 FB                 AND     #$FB	; Save a copy of port B with PB2 low.
01504  00863F  AA                    TAX
01505  008640  09 04                 ora     #$04	; Set PB2 high.
01506  008642  8D E0 7F              STA     SYSTEM_VIA_IOB
01507  
01508          ; Set all bits on port A to outputs. This causes the pin outputs
01509          ; to be set to what we wrote to port A earlier in the subroutine.
01510  008645  A9 FF                 lda     #$FF
01511  008647  8D E3 7F              STA     SYSTEM_VIA_DDRA
01512  
01513          ; Wait for the port A outputs to settle. The datasheet says this
01514          ; must be held at least 20 ns before PB2 (TUSB_WR) is brought low.
01515  00864A  EA                    NOP
01516  00864B  EA                    NOP
01517  
01518          ; Write the original port B value back, setting PB2 back to low.
01519  00864C  8E E0 7F              STX     SYSTEM_VIA_IOB
01520  
01521          ; Read port A. But why? The values read should be the actual
01522          ; values driven on the pins, which may not be what we commanded
01523          ; them to if, for example, they are heavily loaded. This value
01524          ; is returned in the A register, and could be examined by the
01525          ; caller. But this is not used anywhere in the monitor.
01526  00864F  AD E1 7F              LDA     SYSTEM_VIA_IOA
01527  
01528          ; Set all bits in port A as inputs.
01529  008652  A2 00                 ldx     #$00
01530  008654  8E E3 7F              STX     SYSTEM_VIA_DDRA
01531  
01532          ; All done.
01533  008657  60                    rts
01534  
01535  ; A subroutine which does absolutely nothing.
01536  Do_Nothing_Subroutine_1:
01537  008658  60                    rts
01538  
01539  ; Delays by looping 256*X times.
01540  Delay_Loop:
01541  008659  DA                    phx
01542  00865A  A2 00                 ldx     #$00
01543  .loop_256_times:
01544  00865C  CA                    dex
01545  00865D  D0 FD                 bne     .loop_256_times
01546  00865F  FA                    plx
01547  008660  CA                    dex
01548  008661  D0 F6                 bne     Delay_Loop
01549  008663  60                    rts
01550  
01551  ; Saves the current VIA PCR state into work-RAM. This is done after running
01552  ; user code, and before modifying PCR once returning to the monitor. This is
01553  ; necessary in case the user modifies PCR, for example, to control the active
01554  ; banks on the FLASH.
01555  Save_VIA_PCR_State:
01556  008664  AD EC 7F              lda     SYSTEM_VIA_PCR
01557  008667  8D 1C 7E              sta     RAM_PCR_SAVE
01558  00866A  60                    rts
01559  
01560  ; Restores the state of the system VIA's PCR register to what it was when
01561  ; the monitor interrupted the user's code.
01562  Restore_VIA_PCR_State:
01563  00866B  AD 1C 7E              lda     RAM_PCR_SAVE
01564  00866E  8D EC 7F              sta     SYSTEM_VIA_PCR
01565  008671  60                    rts
01566  
01567  ; The second subroutine which does absolutely nothing.
01568  Do_Nothing_Subroutine_2:
01569  008672  60                    rts
01570  
01571  ; The third subroutine which does absolutely nothing.
01572  Do_Nothing_Subroutine_3:
01573  008673  60                    rts
01574  008674  60                    rts
01575  008675  60                    rts
01576  008676  60                    RTS
01577
